The content is a travel itinerary for Estonia that is 5 to 7 days long. It includes information on what to do and see in the country, as well as some travel tips and resources.

To get a feel for Estonia, it's recommended to spend at least 5 to 7 days in the country. This itinerary will take you to some of the highlights of the country, including Tallinn, Lahemaa National Park, Tartu, Saaremaa, and more. It's important to plan your trip carefully to make the most of your time in this beautiful Baltic nation.

If you have 5 days in Estonia, you have the flexibility to explore the city of Tallinn, take a day trip to the surrounding area, visit Tartu, Saaremaa, or Parnu, or spend a week exploring the country. If you are only planning on visiting Estonia, you will likely be arriving into the capital city of Tallinn, which has an international airport and direct connections with Helsinki, Finland, and some other European destinations. It's also possible to arrive via ferry.

Estonia is well-connected to neighboring countries via ferry, bus, and car. If you are only spending 5 days in Estonia and plan to visit Tallinn and Tartu, public transport is a convenient option. For those who want more flexibility and to get off the beaten path, renting a car and planning an Estonia road trip is recommended. Rentalcars.com can be browsed to compare prices across different rental companies. The itinerary for 5 to 7 days in Estonia includes visiting Tallinn on the first day and exploring the city's Old Town.

Tallinn is a well-preserved medieval old town that offers a range of experiences for visitors. Spend a few hours exploring the UNESCO World Heritage Old Town and learn about its history, visit the Town Hall Square, Alexander Nevsky Cathedral, and Patkuli Viewing Platform. Afterwards, head outside of the old town to explore the trendy Kalamaja neighborhood and the Telliskivi Creative City. For accommodations, consider Citybox Tallinn, Savoy Boutique Hotel, Bob W Telliskivi, or Fat Margaret's Hostel. On day two, visit the harbor and Linnahall center.

Tallinn's City Walls

On day four of this itinerary, it's time to hit the road and visit the country's second-largest city of Tartu. This small city is often overlooked, but it is absolutely charming and well worth exploring. Spend your first day in Tartu wandering around the lovely old town. Take in the top sites, climb the tower of St John's Church and even visit the Tartu Botanical Garden before strolling along the beautiful Emajogi River. Then, wander a bit away from the Old Town to the Karlova neighborhood. This is a cool, alternative place with lots of art and some beautiful wooden houses. Here, you can find the trendy Aparaaditehas complex, which is reminiscent of Telliskivi in Tallinn. This former Soviet widget factory has a lot of shops and restaurants that are worth visiting.

For those looking for a good mid-range option in Tartu, Hotel Soho is a great choice. They have clean and comfortable rooms on offer and there is also breakfast included in the nightly rate. If you'd like to have your own place while visiting Tartu, TartuKodu Riia is an excellent choice. Centrally located, the flat is fully furnished and a great place to base yourself when exploring Estonia's second city. Looming Hostel is a good option for those travelling solo or on a budget. Located across the street from Aparaaditehas, they have both dorm and private rooms on offer, good common areas, and a nice roof terrace. It is also possible to purchase breakfast at an extra cost.

On your second day in Tartu and your final day in the country, take the time to dig a little bit deeper in the city and visit a couple of museums.

For a traveler spending 5 days in Estonia, it is recommended to visit the KGB Cells Museum and the Estonian Printing and Paper Museum in Tartu on Day 5, and then spend Day 6 on the beautiful island of Saaremaa. The traveler can reach Saaremaa via car ferry from Virtsu or bus from Tartu to Kuressaare.
